Side NCAP MDB - F1 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
APPENDIX F 
 
Determining the H-Point Location


## Page 301

Side NCAP MDB - F2 
 
 
Determining the H-Point Location for the Driver Seating Position 
 
Position the three-dimensional H-point manikin (i.e., H-point machine) specified in Society of 
Automotive Engineers (SAE) Surface Vehicle Standard J826, revised July 1995, Devices for Use 
in Defining and Measuring Vehicle Seating Accommodation in the seat as follows: 
 
(1) 
Place a 910 mm2 piece of muslin cotton cloth over the seat area.  The muslin cloth shall 
be comparable to 48 threads/in2 and density of 2.85 lb/yd.  Tuck the muslin cloth in a 
sufficient amount to prevent hammocking of the material. 
 
(2) 
Place the seat and back assembly of the H-point machine such that its plane of symmetry 
is coincident with the longitudinal centerline marking on the seat. 
 
(3) 
Install the lower leg and foot segments. 
 
(4) 
Set the length of the lower leg segment at 414 mm (16.3 in) and the length of the thigh 
bar at 401 mm (15.8 in). 
 
(5) 
Leg and foot placement. 
 
 
 
(a) 
Insert the pin so that the foot angle is not less than 87°. 
 
(b) 
Place the right foot on the undepressed accelerator pedal with the sole of the foot 
on the pedal and the heel as far forward as allowable.  Do not place the heel on 
the toe board. 
 
(c) 
Adjust the left leg to be the same distance from the H-point machine centerline 
as the right leg. 
 
(d) 
With the T-bar level, place the left foot on the toe board with the rearmost point of 
the heel resting on the floor pan as close as possible to the point of intersection 
of the planes described by the toe board and the floor pan and not on the wheel 
well projection.  If the foot cannot be positioned on the toe board, set it on the 
floor pan. 
 
(6) 
Apply the lower leg weights. 
 
(7) 
Apply the thigh weights. 
 
(8) 
Tilt the back pan forward against the forward stop and draw the H-point machine away 
from the seat back using the T-bar. 
 
(9) 
Re-positioning the back pan. 
 
(a) 
Allow the H-point machine to slide rearward until a forward horizontal restraining 
load on the T-bar is no longer required due to the seat pan contacting the seat 
back. 
 
(b) 
Slide the H-point machine rearward by a horizontal rearward load applied at the 
T-bar until the seat pan contacts the seat back. 
 
(10) 
Apply a 10 kg load at the intersection of the hip angle quadrant and the T-bar housing 
along a line from the above intersection to a point just above the thigh bar housing. 
 


## Page 302

Side NCAP MDB - F3 
 
 
(11) 
Again apply a 10 kg load at the intersection of the hip angle quadrant and the T-bar 
housing along a line from the above intersection to a point just above the thigh bar 
housing. 
 
(12) 
Carefully return the back pan to the seat back. 
 
(13) 
Install the right and left buttock weights. 
 
(14) 
Install the eight torso weights alternating the installation between left and right. 
 
(15) 
Tilt the back pan forward until the stop is contacted. 
 
(16) 
Rock the H-point machine from side to side over a 10° arc (5° to each side of the vertical 
centerline) for three complete cycles.  Restrain the T-bar during rocking so that the seat 
pan does not change position.  Minimize any inadvertent exterior loads applied in a 
vertical or fore-aft direction.  The feet are free to move during this rocking motion. 
 
(17) 
Without applying a forward or lateral load, lift the right foot off of the floor the minimum 
amount necessary until no additional forward foot movement is obtained. 
 
(18) 
Lower the right foot until the heel is in contact with the floor pan and the ball of the foot is 
in contact with the floor, toe board, or undepressed accelerator pedal. 
 
(19) 
Without applying a forward or lateral load, lift the left foot off of the floor the minimum 
amount necessary until no additional forward foot movement is obtained. 
 
(20) 
Lower the left foot until the heel is in contact with the floor pan and the ball of the foot is in 
contact with the floor or toe board. 
 
(21) 
If the seat pan is level, proceed to (a).  If it is not, proceed to (b). 
 
(a) 
Apply a sufficient lateral load to the top of the seat back pan to level the H-point 
machine seat pan on the seat. 
 
(b) 
Holding the T-bar to prevent the H-point from sliding forward on the seat cushion, 
return the seat back pan to the seat back. 
 
(22) 
Holding the T-bar to prevent the H-point from sliding forward on the seat cushion, apply 
sufficient rearward force perpendicular to the back angle bar just above the torso weights 
to increase the hip angle 3°.  Minimize the exterior downward or side forces applied to the 
H-point machine.  Release the force.  Repeat this step until the hip angle readout is 
identical.  Complete as many force applications as necessary and record the results. 
 
(23) 
If the H-point machine is level, proceed to (24).  If it is not, go back to (15) and repeat 
steps to re-level the H-point machine. 
 
(24) 
Record the H-point location with respect to the horizontal (X, fore-aft of striker), vertical 
(Z, above/below striker), and angle (torso angle fore/aft). 
 
(25) 
Remove the H-point machine and proceed with dummy placement and positioning. 
 


## Page 303

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
APPENDIX G 
HYBRID III HEAD ANGULAR RATE SENSOR 
POLARITY CHECK PROCEDURE
 


## Page 304

L1 
APPENDIX G - HYBRID III HEAD ANGULAR RATE SENSOR (ARS) 
POLARITY CHECK PROCEDURE 
 
Purpose: 
 
This Appendix provides a practical methodology for checking and documenting the 
polarity of the data channel for each dummy mounted head angular rate sensor (ARS) 
relative to the NHTSA sign convention. Documenting the polarity of channels prior to 
testing serves to increase the confidence that they will record data correctly during an 
event. The polarities in this document are the same as those of the SAE J211. 
 
SAE J211 Procedure: 
 
The body coordinate system used for reference is attached to the dummy and is x positive 
pointing forward, y positive pointing to the right, and z positive pointing down. 
 
To check the polarity of the head ARS, the head and chest must be moved in opposite 
directions to induce a measurable rotational rate. Moving the right ear toward the right 
shoulder should result in a positive ωx. Moving the chin away from the sternum results in 
a positive ωy and moving the chin towards the right shoulder will have a positive ωz. If 
any of these motions do not result in a positive reading, the polarity needs to be changed 
to agree with the sign convention. A sign change in the software may be the simplest 
solution. 
 
Polarity Check Data Sheet for Head Angular Rate Sensors 
Dummy Type:  
Serial No.  
Date: 
Direction Motion 
Polarity 
ωx 
Rotate right ear toward right shoulder 
+ (positive) 
ωy 
Rotate chin away from sternum 
+ (positive) 
ωz 
Rotate chin toward right shoulder 
+ (positive)

## Page 307

Side NCAP MDB - H2 
1. PURPOSE AND APPLICATION 
The New Car Assessment Program’s (NCAP’s) side impact moving deformable barrier 
(MDB) test procedure is based on a related safety standard, Federal Motor Vehicle Safety 
Standard (FMVSS) No. 214, which specifies performance requirements for the protection 
of vehicle occupants in crashes. The assessment of certain FMVSS-related parameters 
during NCAP testing allows the Office of Crashworthiness Standards (OCWS) to gain 
supplemental information on the test vehicle. 
 
NOTE: All variables are to be evaluated at NCAP’s 38.5mph (61.90km/h) 
side impact MDB test vehicle velocity.  
 
This document is an appendix to the main side impact MDB laboratory test procedure 
provided by the National Highway Traffic Safety Administration (NHTSA), Office of 
Crashworthiness Standards (OCWS) for the purpose of presenting guidelines for a 
uniform testing data and information recording format, and providing suggestions for the 
use of specific equipment and procedures for contracted testing laboratories. The data 
correspond to requirements for indicant testing in accords with FMVSS No. 301 and 305. 
The OCWS test procedure is not intended to limit or restrain a contractor from 
developing or utilizing any testing techniques or equipment that will assist in procuring 
the required test data. However, applicability of any such testing technique or equipment 
is subject to prior approval by the COR. 
 
The indicant test procedures presented in this appendix are applicable to vehicles tested 
under the main side impact MDB NCAP test procedure. It is the contractor’s 
responsibility to follow the most updated versions of all related test procedures when 
conducting these assessments as part of side impact MDB NCAP testing. These vehicles 
must also meet the requirements set forth in this Appendix.  
 
Vehicles will be tested to the requirements contained herein in conjunction with the 
dynamic requirements for side impact MDB NCAP tests. The test facility must be able to 
conduct these NCAP tests. The facility must meet the minimum requirements regarding 
weighing capability, speed measurement systems, test surface, tow-road, abort system, 
barriers, and all other requirements. 
 
2. DEFINITIONS 
See main SINCAP MDB Procedure, Section 10 for additional Definitions. 
 
DAYLIGHT OPENING (DLO)  
Maximum unobstructed opening through the glazing surface (windshield), including 
reveal or garnish moldings adjoining the surface, as measured parallel to the outer surface 
of the glazing material. 
 
ELECTROLYTE SPILLAGE 
The fall, flow, or run of propulsion battery electrolyte in, on, or from the vehicle, 
including wetness resulting from capillary action. 


## Page 308

Side NCAP MDB - H3 
 
FORWARD CONTROL VEHICLE (FCV)  
Configuration in which more than half of the engine length is rearward of the foremost 
point of the windshield base and the steering wheel hub is in the forward quarter of the 
vehicle length. 
 
PROPULSION BATTERY SYSTEM COMPONENT 
Any part of a propulsion battery module, interconnect, venting system, battery restraint 
device, and battery box or container that holds the individual battery modules used for 
propulsion. 
 
3. PRE-TEST REQUIREMENTS  
3.1. 
DETAILED TEST AND QUALITY CONTROL PROCEDURES REQUIRED 
 
Prior to conducting the indicant test, if requested by the COR, the Contractor may be 
required to submit a detailed in-house test procedure (to the COR) that includes: 
 
a. A step-by-step description of the methodology to be used. 
b. A written Quality Control (QC) Procedure which shall include calibrations, the data 
review process, report review, and the people assigned to perform QC on each task. 
c. A complete listing of test equipment with instrument accuracy and calibration dates. 
d. Detailed check off lists to be used during the test and during data review. These lists 
shall include all test procedure requirements and any additional requirements 
pertaining to the applicable safety standard for which testing is being performed. 
Each separate check off sheet shall identify the laboratory, test date, vehicle, and test 
technicians. These check sheets shall be used to document that all requirements and 
procedures have been complied with. If requested, these sheets shall be submitted 
with the test report. 
e. There shall be no contradiction between the OCWS Laboratory Test Procedure and 
the Contractor's in-house test procedure. 
 
4. FMVSS No. 301 INDICANT TEST 
4.1. 
GENERAL REQUIREMENTS 
This indicant test is based on FMVSS No. 301, which specifies performance requirements 
for the integrity of motor vehicle fuel systems. It is the contractor’s responsibility to follow 
the most updated test procedure when conducting this assessment as part of NCAP testing. 
 
1. 
SIDE MOVING DEFORMABLE BARRIER IMPACT 
When a vehicle is subject to a side impact MDB NCAP test, the following fuel 
leakage conditions must be met: 
 
 
 


## Page 309

Side NCAP MDB - H4 
TIME 
MAX. FLUID SPILLAGE 
From impact until vehicle motion ceases 
1 ounce by weight 
For 5 minute period after vehicle motion ceases 
5 ounces by weight 
For the next 25 minutes 
1 ounce by weight/minute 
 
2. 
STATIC ROLLOVER 
After a vehicle is subject to a side impact MDB NCAP test and placed on a static 
rollover machine, the following fuel leakage conditions must be met: 
 
TIME 
MAX. FLUID SPILLAGE 
For 5 minute period from onset of rotation at each 
90° position 
5 ounces by weight 
For 6th minute  
1 ounce by weight 
For 7th minute (if required) 
1 ounce by weight 
For 8th minute (if required) 
1 ounce by weight 
 
4.2. 
FACILITY AND EQUIPMENT – PRE-TEST REQUIREMENTS) 
1. 
STATIC ROLLOVER MACHINE 
The Contractor must have a rollover machine capable of rotating the barrier-
impacted test vehicle about its longitudinal axis with the axis kept horizontal, to 
each successive increment of 90°, 180°, and 270° at a uniform rate, with 90° of 
rotation taking place in any time interval from 1 to 3 minutes.  
 
 
2. 
STODDARD COLLECTION CONTAINERS AND STOPWATCH 
Containers for the collection of Stoddard solvent and a calibrated stopwatch for 
timing the fluid collection intervals are required. Leakage will be collected for the 5 
minute period from the beginning of rotation plus any additional 1 minute 
collection periods that are required. Containers must be labeled before they are 
photographed. 
 
3. 
OTHER TEST INSTRUMENTATION 
The Contractor shall provide the necessary equipment to permanently record and 
display data. The data shall be included in the final test report and on the electronic 
data media. 
 
4.3. 
FUEL SYSTEM INTEGRITY PROCEDURE 
After the vehicle impact, fuel system Stoddard solvent leakage (if any) should be 
collected by hand and documented with a real-time (24-30 fps) video camera and 
stopwatch. The “tea cup method” involves simply placing a collection vessel beneath the 
leakage source and timing the intervals of several collected volumes. The collected 


## Page 310

Side NCAP MDB - H5 
Stoddard solvent samples can subsequently be measured and spillage rates calculated. If 
the “tea cup method” is used, the test personnel must be in position to reach observation 
points around the test vehicle at the instant the vehicle comes to rest after the impact 
event. 
 
 
NOTE: It is the Contractor’s responsibility to collect any suspect liquids 
leaking from the vehicle post-test and analyze the contents if 
necessary. 
 
 
4.4. 
STATIC ROLLOVER PROCEDURE 
The Contractor must conduct a static rollover test within 30 minutes after the vehicle 
impact. The Contractor must keep the test vehicle under constant observation for 
Stoddard solvent leakage during the transition between impact and static rollover testing. 
 
When the test vehicle is rotated in a fixture on its longitudinal axis to each successive 
increment of 90°, following an impact crash, Stoddard solvent spillage, from the onset of 
rotational motion, shall not exceed a total of 5 ounces by weight for the first 5 minutes of 
testing at each successive 90° increment. For the remaining testing period, at each 
increment of 90°, solvent spillage during any l-minute interval shall not exceed 1ounce 
by weight. 
 
4.5. 
STATIC ROLLOVER TEST CONDITIONS 
Prior to conducting any static rollover test, ATDs should be removed from the vehicle. 
Within 30 minutes of vehicle impact, the Contractor should place the vehicle in the test 
fixture where it may be rotated in a test fixture about its longitudinal axis, with the axis 
kept horizontal, to each successive increment of the following: 
 
Rotation 1 - 90° 
Rotation 2 - 180° 
Rotation 3 - 270° 
Rotation 4 - 360° 
 
Rotation 1 must be done such that the vehicle’s fuel filler cap or plug is on the bottom of 
the vehicle when the rotation is completed. Rotation must take place at a uniform rate, 
with 90° of rotation taking place in any time interval from 1 to 3 minutes. After reaching 
each 90° increment, the vehicle is held in that position for 5 minutes. 
 
Leakage will be collected for the 5-minute period from the beginning of rotation plus up 
to three 1-minute collection periods. Containers for the collection of possible Stoddard 
solvent spillage and a calibrated stopwatch for timing the fluid collection intervals are 
required. Containers must be labeled before they are photographed. 
 
The Contractor should complete Data Sheet No. 14 in Appendix E of the main side 
impact MDB NCAP procedure and include it with the test report. 
 


## Page 311

Side NCAP MDB - H6 
 
5.  FMVSS No. 305 INDICANT TEST 
5.1. 
GENERAL REQUIREMENTS 
This indicant test is based on FMVSS No. 305, which specifies performance 
requirements for the limitation of electrolyte spillage, retention of propulsion batteries, 
and electrical isolation of the chassis from the high-voltage system during the crash 
event. It applies to vehicles that use electricity as propulsion power. 
 
It is the contractor’s responsibility to follow the most updated test procedure when 
conducting this assessment as part of NCAP testing. 
 
When a vehicle is subject to a side impact MDB NCAP test,), it shall NOT: 
a. Spill more than 5.0 liters of electrolyte from propulsion batteries outside the 
passenger compartment, and no visible trace of electrolyte shall spill into the 
passenger compartment. Spillage is measured from the time the vehicle ceases 
motion after a barrier impact test until 30 minutes thereafter, and throughout any 
static rollover after a barrier impact test.  
b. Have any propulsion battery system component located inside the passenger 
compartment move from the location in which they are installed. 
c. Have any propulsion battery system component located outside the passenger 
compartment enter the passenger compartment. 
d. Fail to maintain an electrical isolation of no less than 500 ohms/volt between the 
propulsion battery system and the vehicle’s electricity-conducting structure. 
 
5.2. 
FACILITY AND EQUIPMENT: PRE-TEST REQUIREMENTS 
1. 
VOLTAGE MEASUREMENT DEVICE AND INTERFACE 
The voltmeter used in this test shall measure AC and DC values and have an 
internal impedance of at least 10MΩ. 
 
Voltage measurements throughout this test must be made quickly and safely. To 
ensure these requirements are met, the testing lab must devise, for COR approval, a 
test interface port or other device to facilitate these voltage measurements. All 
voltage measurements shall be immediate upon connection to the interface port. 
This test interface port equipment shall be easily accessible from the exterior of the 
vehicle and connected to the appropriate propulsion system and battery components 
via laboratory installed wires. The external mounting of this test interface port shall 
be configured such that no movement, interference, or damage will result to it from 
a barrier crash test. The test interface port shall incorporate a fusible link and any 
other necessary safety device or usage procedure to protect the data measurement 
and recording equipment from damage, and the test technicians from electrical 
shock. 
 
A terminal block or circuit board is recommended as a means to providing an 
external interface  


## Page 312

Side NCAP MDB - H7 
 
The following is an example quoted from Transport Canada document, “Test 
Procedures, Frontal Impact 208-212-301F-305F, No. 03-002” 
 
“This kit is composed of a PVC box compliant with the electrical code and 
containing insulated banana connectors that allow the measuring equipment to 
be connected for the verification of the standard. A warning light indicates the 
presence of voltage inside the box. A shielded cable with three conductors, 20 
feet in length and capable of supporting 600 volts, connects the box to the 
vehicle’s electrical system. This cable is covered with orange-colored 
mechanical protection (similar to the Hybrid vehicle high-voltage 
identification code). The box is protected by a 0.5-amp fuse. 
 
2. 
STATIC ROLLOVER MACHINE 
The rollover machine must be capable of rotating, and holding in place, the 
impacted NCAP test vehicle up to 5443 kg about its longitudinal axis with the axis 
kept horizontal, to each successive increment of 90°, 180°, and 270° at a uniform 
rate, with 90° of rotation taking place in any time interval from 1 to 3 minutes. 
Leakage will be collected for the 5-minute period from the beginning of rotation 
plus any additional 1-minute collection periods that are required. Voltage 
measurements shall be able to be made continuously throughout the rollover test. 
 
3. 
STODDARD AND ELECTROLYTE COLLECTION CONTAINERS AND 
STOPWATCH 
Containers for the collection of Stoddard solvent and propulsion battery electrolyte 
and a calibrated stopwatch for timing the fluid collection intervals are required. 
Containers for each fluid collected must be labeled before they are photographed. 
For containers containing both Stoddard and electrolyte, the fluids should be 
allowed to separate by specific gravity then measured and photographed. 
 
4. 
OTHER TEST INSTRUMENTATION 
The Contractor shall provide the necessary equipment to permanently record and 
display data. The data shall be included in the final test report and on the electronic 
data media. 
 
5.3. 
ELECTROLYTE SPILLAGE AND ELECTRICAL SHOCK PROTECTION PROCEDURE 
1. 
DATA COLLECTION SET-UP  
a. Remove the key from the keylock and ensure the vehicle is not powered.  
b. Remove barriers to access the propulsion battery module (e.g. seat backs, 
carpet, covers).  
c. Wear high-voltage protection gloves, nonconductive shoes, eye protection 
and any other safety equipment deemed necessary to safely prepare the 
vehicle and conduct the test.  
d. Set the propulsion battery module switch, service plug, or otherwise to the 
“OFF” or depowered, position (See Figure 1H below). Follow any 
Manufacturer instructions provided by the COR. Wait 5 minutes. 


## Page 313

Side NCAP MDB - H8 
 
 
Figure 1H: Examples of Service Switches and Plugs 
 
e. Remove propulsion battery module service cover, or cover that closes the 
battery compartment.  
f. Measure the voltage across the propulsion battery at the appropriate 
terminals, and verify 0 volts.  
g. Measure the voltage between the positive terminal of the propulsion battery 
and the vehicle body, and verify 0 volts.  
h. Measure the voltage between the negative terminal of the propulsion battery 
and the vehicle body, and verify 0 volts.  
i. If any voltage measurements differ from 0 volts, STOP, quarantine vehicle, 
document incident and contact the COTR.  
j. Attach test leads from the propulsion battery, propulsion system, automatic 
propulsion battery disconnect, ground points, and any other points necessary 
on the vehicle such that immediate retrieval of data is possible after an impact 
event and at all times during the static rollover test. 
 
NOTE: If vehicle is equipped with an automatic disconnect physically 
contained within the battery pack system, all voltage measurements 
after impact will be taken from the traction side of the automatic 
disconnect to the vehicle chassis. 
 
If the vehicle utilizes an automatic disconnect that is not physically 
contained within the battery pack system, all post-impact voltage 
measurements are to be made from the battery side of the automatic 
disconnect. Automatic disconnect presence, location, and set-up 
instruction is vehicle-specific, and is available from the COTR.  
 
k. Re-install the propulsion battery module service cover, or otherwise close the 
battery compartment. Take great care to preserve the integrity of the 
connection wiring and propulsion battery hold-downs.  
 
2. 
TEST VEHICLE PREPARATION 
a. Apply paint or other highly visible finish, such as machinist blue, to all 
battery system component attachment fasteners or attachment means (e.g., 
Service Plug – Toyota Prius 
  
Service Switch – Honda Civic 
Service Switch – Ford Escape 


## Page 314

Side NCAP MDB - H9 
welds), to indicate component movement or separation after the governing 
NCAP barrier test.  
b. If the vehicle is equipped with a liquid cooling system, assure that the coolant 
is a different color than the Stoddard solvent in use. 
c. Reset the propulsion battery module switch, service plug, or otherwise to the 
“ON”, or powered, position. Verify proper function of propulsion system.  
d. Charge the propulsion battery system to:  
 
1. The maximum state of charge recommended by the manufacturer, as 
stated in the vehicle Owner’s Manual, or on a label that is permanently 
affixed to the vehicle; 
OR  
2. A state of charge of not less than 95 percent of the maximum capacity of 
the battery system, if the manufacturer has made no recommendation. 
Maximum capacity can be verified by consulting the COR;  
 OR  
3. The maximum practicable state of charge within the normal operating 
range, as specified by the manufacturer, and as indicated by the vehicle’s 
instrumentation, if the batteries are rechargeable only by an energy source 
on the vehicle. Discuss with COR prior to operating the vehicle.  
e. 
Complete Data Sheets No. 305-1 and No. 305-2 in Appendix E. 
f. 
Prepare the test vehicle per the remainder of this test procedure. 
g. 
Document and photograph the test vehicle per the requirements set forth in 
this test procedure. 
 
3. 
ELECTRICAL ISOLATION BASELINE MEASUREMENT 
NOTE: The following measurements are to be made immediately prior to the 
crash test, and should be completed within 15 minutes. 
 
a. Check that the battery system is connected to the vehicle’s propulsion system, 
and the vehicle is in the “ready-to-drive” (propulsion motor(s) activated) 
position. Start Data Sheet No. 305-3 in Appendix E.  
b. Measure the voltage of the propulsion battery as shown in Figure 2H. Before 
any vehicle impact test, verify that Vb is equal to or greater than the nominal 
operating voltage, as specified by the vehicle manufacturer, or as supplied by 
the COR. If Vb is not equal to or greater than the nominal operating voltage, as 
specified by the vehicle manufacturer, or as supplied by the COR, repeat the 
propulsion battery charging Step d of Item 2 Test Vehicle Preparation and 
promptly call the COR for guidance. The voltmeter used in this test measures 
direct current values and has an internal impedance of at least 10MΩ. Record 
the voltage measurement as Vb on Data Sheet No. 305-3 in Appendix E. 
Make certain all voltages are DC. If there is AC voltage on the traction side 
connection, consult the COR for additional guidance.  


## Page 315

Side NCAP MDB - H10 
 
Figure 2H 
  
c. Measure the voltage (V1) from the negative side of the propulsion battery to 
the vehicle chassis point(s) as shown in Figure 3H. Record the voltage 
measurement as V1, on Data Sheet No. 305-3 in Appendix E.  
 
Figure 3H 
  
d. Measure the voltage (V2) from the positive side of the propulsion battery to 
the vehicle chassis point(s) as shown in Figure 4H. Record the voltage 
measurement as V2, on Data Sheet No. 305-3 in Appendix E.

the nominal operating voltage of the vehicle (in volts) per SAE J1766, 
between the negative side of the propulsion battery and the vehicle chassis. 
With Ro installed, measure and record the voltage (V1 ') as shown in Figure

5H between the negative side of the propulsion battery and the vehicle chassis

NOTE: Ro is not required to be precisely this value since the equations 
are valid for any Ro; however, an Ro value in this range should 
provide good resolution for the voltage measurements.1  
 
Figure 5H

point(s). Calculate the electrical isolation value (in ohms) as shown in Figure 
6H. 
 
NOTE: If the measured voltage is zero and results in a division by 
zero in the electrical isolation calculation, record “Zero 
Volts.” This “zero voltage” condition is considered as being 
compliant.

NOTE: The exact location of measurement will vary depending on 
the location of the disconnect(s) for the system.  
 
g. If Ri1 is less than Ri2 then, divide Ri1 by the nominal operating voltage of the 
propulsion battery (Vb) shown in Figure 5H.  
 
NOTE: If the measured voltage is zero and results in a division by 
zero, record “Zero Volts.” This “zero voltage” condition is 
considered as being compliant.  
 
Record this value as Ri / Vb, on Data Sheet No. 305-3 in Appendix E. This 
value must be equal to or greater than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test 
failure has occurred. 
h. If Ri2 is less than Ri1 then, divide Ri2 by the nominal operating voltage of the 
propulsion battery (Vb) shown in Figure 5H.  
 
NOTE: If the measured voltage is zero and results in a division by 
zero, record “Zero Volts.” This “zero voltage” condition is 
considered as being compliant.  
 
Record this value as Ri / Vb, on Data Sheet No. 305-3 in Appendix E. This 
value must be equal to or greater than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test 
failure has occurred. 
i. Recheck that the battery system is connected to the vehicle’s propulsion 
system, and that the vehicle in the “ready-to-drive” (propulsion motor(s) 
activated) position.  
j. Verify that the parking brake and transmission are set in accordance with this 
side impact MDB NCAP procedure.  
k. Perform the side impact MDB NCAP test. 
 


## Page 318

Side NCAP MDB - H13 
NOTE: If the vehicle is equipped with an automatic disconnect 
physically contained within the battery pack system, all 
voltage measurements after impact will be taken from the 
traction side of the automatic disconnect to the vehicle chassis. 
  
If the vehicle utilizes an automatic disconnect that is not 
physically contained within the battery pack system, all post-
impact voltage measurements are to be made from the battery 
side of the automatic disconnect. Automatic disconnect 
presence, location, and set-up instruction is vehicle specific 
and must be obtained from the COTR. 
 
4. 
ELECTRICAL ISOLATION COMPLIANCE MEASUREMENT 
NOTE: All voltage measurements shall be recorded immediately after the 
governing NCAP barrier impact test, and at the start of each 
increment of 90º, 180º, 270º, and 360º of the FMVSS No. 301 indicant 
static rollover test. 
  
NOTE: If the measured voltage is zero and results in a division by zero, 
record “Zero Volts.” This “zero voltage” condition is considered as 
being compliant.  
  
a. Immediately following the crash test, measure V1, V2, V1 ', and V2 ' voltages per 
Figure 6H with Ro installed and record the values on Data Sheet No. 305-4 
in Appendix E.  
b. Calculate the electrical isolation value (in ohms) as shown in Figure 5H. 
Record the electrical isolation value as Ri1 on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in 
Appendix E.  
c. Calculate the electrical isolation value (in ohms) as shown in Figure 6H. 
Record the electrical isolation value as Ri2 on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in 
Appendix E. 
d. If Ri1 is less than Ri2 then, divide Ri1 by the nominal operating voltage of the 
propulsion battery (Vb) shown in Figure 5H. Record this value as Ri / Vb, on 
Data Sheet No. 305-4 in Appendix E. This value must be equal to or greater 
than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test failure has occurred. 
e. 
If Ri2 is less than Ri1 then, divide Ri2 by the nominal operating voltage of the 
propulsion battery (Vb) shown in Figure 5H. Record this value as Ri / Vb, on 
Data Sheet No. 305-4 in Appendix E. This value must be equal to or greater 
than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test failure has occurred. 
f. Visually inspect for electrolyte leakage in the passenger compartment and 
record and photograph findings on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in Appendix E. 
Additional photographs to document such findings should be included per the 
requirements set forth in the Photographic Documentation section in 
Appendix E. 


## Page 319

Side NCAP MDB - H14 
g. Visually inspect for external battery component entry into the occupant 
compartment and record and photograph findings on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in 
Appendix E. 
h. Visually inspect for internal battery component movement in the occupant 
compartment and record and photograph findings on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in 
Appendix E. Additional photographs to document such findings should be 
included per the requirements set forth in the Photographic Documentation 
section in Appendix E. 
i. Photograph the test vehicle per the deliverables outlined in the governing 
NCAP barrier test procedure and in this test procedure and record any 
additional findings in the applicable data sheets.  
j. Prepare the vehicle for the static rollover test by following Section 6 (FMVSS 
No. 301 Indicant Test) of this Appendix. 
 
5. 
STATIC ROLLOVER TEST 
NOTE: When the test vehicle is rotated in a fixture on its longitudinal axis to 
each successive increment of 90o following the side impact NCAP 
test, propulsion battery electrolyte leakage shall not exceed 5 liters. 
 
Additionally, electrical isolation shall not be less than 500 ohms/volt 
throughout the side impact NCAP test or at each 90o increment of the 
static rollover test. 
 
The passenger compartment must be visually checked directly after a barrier 
impact for evidence of electrolyte leakage, battery system component 
intrusion, and retention of interior mounted battery modules. Photographs of 
the propulsion battery system components should be taken before the vehicle 
is placed on the static rollover machine. Any ATDs used for governing NCAP 
test should also be removed. 
  
Do not proceed to the static rollover if there are apparent test failures or test 
anomalies of the NCAP barrier test. The Contractor must conduct a static 
rollover test within 45 minutes after the vehicle impact only after the 
Quicklook Report provides assurance that the vehicle has met the performance 
requirements of the applicable frontal, side MDB, or side pole NCAP barrier 
test, and also the requirements outlined by FMVSS No. 301 and 305 indicant 
tests that must be met prior to the static rollover test. The Contractor must 
keep the test vehicle under constant observation for propulsion battery 
electrolyte leakage during the transition between barrier impact and static 
rollover testing. 
  
After the vehicle impact, any propulsion battery electrolyte leakage shall be 
collected by hand and documented with a real time (24 fps) digital motion 
picture camera. Like FMVSS 301 indicant testing, the "tea cup method" may 
be used to collect electrolyte spillage from any leakage source(s), though 
Contractors are invited to suggest alternative methods for fluid collection. The 


## Page 320

Side NCAP MDB - H15 
collected propulsion battery electrolyte samples can subsequently be measured 
and spillage volume calculated. If the "tea cup method" is used, the test 
personnel must be in position to reach observation points around the test 
vehicle at the instant the vehicle comes to rest after the impact event. If 
possible, the collections of Stoddard solvent, propulsion battery electrolyte, or 
any other fluids should be segregated (if leakage of fluids is present). If it is 
not possible to collect leakage samples separately, provide a collection vessel 
that is adequately sized to collect the leakage mixture and separate by suitable 
means, post-test. Take adequate safeguards when collecting leakage, as it may 
be hazardous.  
  
a. Reference static rollover preparation and procedure from Section 6 (FMVSS 
No. 301 Indicant Test) of this Appendix. 
b. Mount the test vehicle on the static rollover fixture and position at 0o (wheels 
down). 
c. Immediately following the rollover transition of each successive increment of 
90o (e.g. at 90o, 180o, 270o, 360o), perform the following: 
  
NOTE: If measured voltage is zero and results in a division by zero, 
record “Zero Volts.” This “zero voltage” condition is 
considered as being compliant.  
 
i. Measure V1, V2, V1 ', and V2 ' voltages per Figures 3H -6H with Ro 
installed, and record the values on Data Sheet No. 305-5 in Appendix E. 
ii. Calculate the electrical isolation value (in ohms) as shown in Figure 5H. 
Record the electrical isolation value as Ri1 on Data Sheet No. 305-5 in 
Appendix E. 
iii. Calculate the electrical isolation value (in ohms) as shown in Figure 6H. 
Record the electrical isolation value as Ri2 on Data Sheet No. 305-5 in 
Appendix E. 
iv. If Ri1 is less than Ri2 then, divide Ri1 by the nominal operating voltage of 
the propulsion battery (Vb) shown in Figure 5H. Record this value as Ri / 
Vb, on Data Sheet No. 305-5 in Appendix E. This value must be equal to 
or greater than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test failure has 
occurred. 
v. If Ri2 is less than Ri1 then, divide Ri2 by the nominal operating voltage of 
the propulsion battery (Vb) shown in Figure 5H. Record this value as Ri / 
Vb, on Data Sheet No. 305-5 in Appendix E. This value must be equal to 
or greater than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test failure has 
occurred. 
d. Repeat Step c for increments of 180o, 270o, and 360o. 
 
6. 
POST-ROLLOVER REQUIREMENTS 
a.  After the required tests are completed, the Contractor shall: 
i. Verify all data sheets are complete and take any remaining photographs.  


## Page 321

Side NCAP MDB - H16 
ii. Complete the Report of Vehicle Condition, found in Appendix E. Include 
a word description of the vehicle’s post-test condition. 
iii. Copy applicable pages of the Vehicle Owner’s Manual for attachment to 
the test reports. 
iv. Remove all instrumentation from vehicle. Return vehicle to its pre-test 
condition and move the test vehicle to a secure area.  
v. Place all original records in a secure and organized file to await test data 
disposition.

## Page 325

Side NCAP MDB - I1 
 
DELIBERATIVE PROPOSED DRAFT 
OVERVIEW 
 
Summary.  NHTSA has developed an alteration to the SID-IIsD side impact dummy for the 
installation of an instrumentation package within the dummy’s head.  This alteration improves 
the utility of the dummy as a test tool.  This alteration does not change the dummy in any way 
other than to improve its usability and objectivity.1  This document also describes an alteration to 
the regulatory text that serves to correct a minor error in the qualification procedure for the iliac 
test.   
 
Description of alterations.  The alterations are described below. 
 
I.  Instrumentation for the head assembly.  This alteration involves the installation of an 
instrumentation package consisting of three accelerometers, three redundant accelerometers, and 
three angular rate sensors (ARS) within the head of the dummy.  The optional instrumentation 
provides a means to monitor brain injury potential without otherwise affecting the performance 
of the dummy.  The redundant accelerometers serve as back-ups in case an unexpected 
malfunction occurs in the primary accelerometers.   
 
II. Iliac impact procedure.  This alteration corrects an error in the qualification procedure for the 
iliac test. The horizontal orientation of the impactor specified in the current regulatory text is 
incorrect.   
 
Current SID-IIsD Specifications.  The SID-IIsD is specified in 49 CFR § Part 572 Subpart V.  
This publication contains regulatory text describing the qualification procedures and 
requirements for the dummy.   Subpart V also incorporates several other documents by reference.  
Those documents describe the physical make-up of the dummy, and include a parts list, a set of 
engineering drawings, and a document entitled, “Procedures for Assembly, Disassembly, and 
Inspection.”  These references reside in docket file NHTSA-2009-0002 found on 
www.regulations.gov.  The full document titles and document numbers are: 
 
• Parts/Drawings List, Part 572 Subpart V, SID-IIsD, July 1, 2008, NHTSA-2009-0002, 
document no. 0022. 
 
• Drawings and Specifications for the SID-IIsD Small Female Crash Test Dummy, Part 572 
Subpart V, Rev. H, July 1, 2008, NHTSA-2009-0002, document no. 0024. 
 
• Procedures for Assembly, Disassembly, and Inspection (PADI) of the SID-IIsD Side Impact 
Crash Test Dummy, July 1, 2008, NHTSA-2009-0002, document no. 0023. 
 
Implementation of alterations.  The information presented herein describes how the current 
Subpart V specifications are affected by the alterations.  Corresponding edits to the Subpart V 
engineering drawings, parts list, regulatory text, and PADI are provided to explain how to 
implement the alterations correctly.    
                                                 
1 Technical Report: 3aω head instrumentation package applied to the HIII-5F and SID-IIsD:  Effects on impact 
response and mass properties of the head, National Highway Traffic Safety Administration, May 2018. 
 


## Page 326

Side NCAP MDB - I2 
 
DELIBERATIVE PROPOSED DRAFT 
 
End-users may implement the alterations at their discretion.  Note that the alterations are not 
interrelated, so there is no special need to implement them concurrently.  Either can be 
implemented without implementing the other.     
 
Relevance to Part 572.  This document does not in any way constitute a revision to the 49 CFR § 
Part 572 Subpart V.  Nor does it constitute a change to any of the components that are 
incorporated into Subpart V by reference, which include the parts list, the engineering drawing 
package, and the PADI. This document serves only to describe how Subpart V is affected by the 
alterations.

Side NCAP MDB - I3 
 
DELIBERATIVE PROPOSED DRAFT 
I.  INSTRUMENTATION FOR THE HEAD ASSEMBLY 
 
1.  Alterations to the Engineering Drawing Package and Parts List.    
 
a.  New drawings added (see Appendix A): 
 
• DL180-1000, Redundant Accelerometers with ARS, SID-IIsD 
• 180-0212R, Mounting plate, SID-IIsD 
• SA572-S79, ARS/Accelerometer Mounting Block 
• SA572-S4984, Redundant Accel. Stacker 
• SA572-S56, Rev. C, Angular Rate Sensor – 8k 
• SA572-S57, Rev. C, Angular Rate Sensor – 12k 
• SA572-S58, Rev. C, Angular Rate Sensor – 18k 
 
b.  Alterations to existing drawings.   
The following drawings are altered to specify an option to install redundant accelerometers and 
angular rate sensors.  
 
• 180-0000, Rev. H, SID-IIsD, Complete Assembly, Sheet 2. 
• 180-0000, Rev. H, SID-IIsD, Complete Assembly, Part Groupings, Sheet 4.   
• 180-1000, Rev. E, 6 Axis Head Assembly. 
 
2.  Alterations to the Subpart V Regulatory Text. 
 
a. Alterations to §572.200 Test conditions and instrumentation. 
 
Insert new paragraph (e): 
 
(e) Optional angular rate sensors for the head, if installed, have the dimensions and response 
characteristics specified in any of drawings SA572-S56, SA572-S57, or SA572-S58.   
 
Former paragraphs (e) and (f) are incremented to (f) and (g). 
 
Former paragraph (g) is incremented to (h) and revised as follows: 
 
(h)  
(1) Head: 
(i) Accelerations – digitally filtered CFC 1000. 
(ii) Angular velocities – digitally filtered CFC 60. 
 
Former paragraphs (h)-(k) are incremented to (i)-(l).

Rename section 6.1.1: 
 
Was:  6.1.1 Installation of Head Accelerometers 
Now:  6.1.1 Installation of Standard Head Instrumentation 
 
At the top of page 70, add instructions and new pictures that describe the order of installation for 
the optional head instrumentation as follows: 
 
6.1.2  Optional:  Procedure for installing redundant accelerometers and angular rate 
sensors. 
 
1.  Install six uniaxial piezoresistive accelerometers and three angular rate sensors on the 
ARS/accelerometer mounting block (SA572-S79) as shown in Fig. 122 by following steps a-f 
below  Mount all sensors by following the right hand rule for signal polarity in accordance with 
the SAE J211.  See Appendix A for further details on sensor polarities. 
 
a. The two x-axis accelerometers are installed on the front of the mounting block using one 
redundant accelerometer stacker placed between two accelerometers and secured to the  
mounting block with two 0-80 x 3/8 SHCS. 
 
b. The x-axis ARS is mounted on the rear of the mounting block using two 0-80 x 3/8 SHCS. 
 
c. The two y-axis accelerometers are installed on the left side of the mounting block using one 
redundant accelerometer stacker placed between two accelerometers and secured to the mounting 
block with two 0-80 x 3/8 SHCS. 
 
d. The y-axis ARS is installed on the right side of the mounting block using two 0-80 x 3/8 
SHCS. 
 
e. The two z-axis accelerometers are installed on the top of the mounting block using one 
redundant accelerometer stacker placed between two accelerometers and secured to the mounting 
block with two 0-80 x 3/8 SHCS. 
 
f. The z-axis ARS is installed in a pocket on the underside of the mounting block with the label 
side of the ARS facing up using two 0-80 x 3/8 SHCS. 
 
2.  Install the ARS/accelerometer mounting block (SA572-S79) using two 2-56 x 5/8 SHCS on 
the mounting plate (part no. 180-0212R) as shown in Fig. 123.   
 
3. Install the mounting plate (part no. 180-0212R), on the upper neck load cell (part no. SA572-
S11) using two 10-24 x 7/16 SHCS and two 10-24 x 3/8 BHCS as shown in Fig. 124. Optionally 
it is a possibility that the neck transducer structural replacement, part no. 180-1003, is being used 
in place of the upper neck load cell. Note: the 10-24 x 3/8 BHCS under the x-axis ARS cannot be 
installed or removed with the ARS/accelerometer mounting block (SA572-S79) installed. 
 


## Page 334

Side NCAP MDB - I10 
 
DELIBERATIVE PROPOSED DRAFT 
4. Place the upper neck load cell with the mounting plate in the head, but do not install; leave it 
loose. 
 
5. Complete the installation of the upper neck load cell as described in Section 6.2.1.

DELIBERATIVE PROPOSED DRAFT 
II.  ILIAC IMPACT TEST SPECIFICATION 
 
1.  Alterations to the Engineering Drawing Package and Parts List.    
No alterations to the regulatory text are needed. 
 
2.  Alterations to the Subpart V Regulatory Text. 
 
Orientation of the iliac impactor.  Edit the regulatory text in S572.199(b)(8) describing the iliac 
impact test procedure.  The horizontal orientation of the impactor specified in the current 
regulatory text is incorrect.  As shown in the diagram below, the 88.9 mm (3.50 inch) dimension 
of the probe's impact surface should be aligned vertically, not horizontally.   
 
 
Figure II.1.  Diagram of iliac impact test described in S572.199(b)(8) showing that the 88.9 mm 
face of the impact probe is aligned vertically.   
 
This is an obvious error in the regulatory text.  The probe is shown in the regulatory text in Fig. 
V9A, Iliac Impact, part number 180-9800.  The full engineering drawing of the probe (shown 
below) is found in:  Qualification Procedures for the SID-IIsD Side Impact Crash Test Dummy, 
July 1, 2008. (See online link: https://www.regulations.gov; search under nhtsa-2009-0002-
0016.).  The edit consists entirely of the following change: 
 
S572.199   Pelvis iliac. 
 (b) 
 (8) The dummy is positioned with respect to the impactor such that the longitudinal centerline of 
the impact probe is in line with the longitudinal centerline of the iliac load cell access hole, and 
the 88.9 mm dimension of the probe's impact surface is aligned horizontally vertically. 
 
3.  Alterations to the PADI.   
No alterations to the PADI are needed.
